whether or not the ownerRules cover the servantRules in terms of allowed actions.\n26: // It returns whether or not the ownerRules cover and a list of the rules that the ownerRules do not cover.\n27: func Covers(ownerRules, servantRules []rbacv1.PolicyRule) (bool, []rbacv1.PolicyRule) {\n28: \t// 1.  Break every servantRule into individual rule tuples: group, verb, resource, resourceName\n29: \t// 2.  Compare the mini-rules against each owner rule.  Because the breakdown is down to the most atomic level, we're guaranteed that each mini-servant rule will be either fully covered or not covered by a single owner rule\n30: \t// 3.  Any left over mini-rules means that we are not covered and we have a nice list of them.\n31: \t// TODO: it might be nice to collapse the list down into something more human readable\n32: \n33: \tsubrules := []rbacv1.PolicyRule{}\n34: \tfor _, servantRule := range servantRules {\n35: \t\tsubrules = append(subrules, BreakdownRule(servantRule)...)\n36: \t}\n37: \n38: \tuncoveredRules := []rbacv1.PolicyRule{}\n39: \tfor _, subrule := range subrules {\n40: \t\tcovered := false\n41: \t\tfor _, ownerRule := range ownerRules {\n42: \t\t\tif ruleCovers(ownerRule, subrule) {\n43: \t\t\t\tcovered = true\n44: \t\t\t\tbreak\n45: \t\t\t}\n46: \t\t}\n47: \n48: \t\tif !covered {\n49: \t\t\tuncoveredRules = append(uncoveredRules, subrule)\n50: \t\t}\n51: \t}\n52: \n53: \treturn (len(uncoveredRules) == 0), uncoveredRules\n54: }\n55: \n56: // BreadownRule takes a rule and builds an equivalent list of rules that each have at most one verb, one\n57: // resource, and one resource name\n58: func BreakdownRule(rule rbacv1.PolicyRule) []rbacv1.PolicyRule {\n59: \tsubrules := []rbacv1.PolicyRule{}\n60: \tfor _, group := range rule.APIGroups {\n61: \t\tfor _, resource := range rule.Resources {\n62: \t\t\tfor _, verb := range rule.Verbs {\n63: \t\t\t\tif len(rule.ResourceNames) > 0 {\n64: \t\t\t\t\tfor _, resourceName := range rule.ResourceNames {\n65: \t\t\t\t\t\tsubrules = append(subrules, rbacv1.PolicyRule{APIGroups: []string{group}, Resources: []string{resource}, Verbs: []string{verb}, ResourceNames: []string{resourceName}})\n66: \t\t\t\t\t}\n67: \n68: \t\t\t\t} else {\n69: \t\t\t\t\tsubrules = append(subrules, rbacv1.PolicyRule{APIGroups: []string{group}, Resources: []string{resource}, Verbs: []string{verb}})\n70: \t\t\t\t}\n71: \n72: \t\t\t}\n73: \t\t}\n74: \t}\n75: \n76: \t// Non-resource URLs are unique because they only combine with verbs.\n77: \tfor _, nonResourceURL := range rule.NonResourceURLs {\n78: \t\tfor _, verb := range rule.Verbs {\n79: \t\t\tsubrules = append(subrules, rbacv1.PolicyRule{NonResourceURLs: []string{nonResourceURL}, Verbs: []string{verb}})\n80: \t\t}\n81: \t}\n82: \n83: \treturn subrules\n84: }\n85: \n86: func has(set []string, ele string) bool {\n87: \tfor _, s := range set {\n88: \t\tif s == ele {\n89: \t\t\treturn true\n90: \t\t}\n91: \t}\n92: \treturn false\n93: }\n94: \n95: func hasAll(set, contains []string) bool {\n96: \towning := make(map[string]struct{}, len(set))\n97: \tfor _, ele := range set {\n98: \t\towning[ele] = struct{}{}\n99: \t}\n100: \tfor _, ele := range contains {\n101: \t\tif _, ok := owning[ele]; !ok {\n102: \t\t\treturn false\n103: \t\t}\n104: \t}\n105: \treturn true\n106: }\n107: \n108: func resourceCoversAll(setResources, coversResources []string) bool {\n109: \t// if we have a star or an exact match on all resources, then we match\n110: \tif has(setResources, rbacv1.ResourceAll) || hasAll(setResources, coversResources) {\n111: \t\treturn true\n112: \t}\n113: \n114: \tfor _, path := range coversResources {\n115: \t\t// if we have an exact match, then we match.\n116: \t\tif has(setResources, path) {\n117: \t\t\tcontinue\n118: \t\t}\n119: \t\t// if we're not a subresource, then we definitely don't match.  fail.\n120: \t\tif !strings.Contains(path, \"/\") {\n121: \t\t\treturn false\n122: \t\t}\n123: \t\ttokens := strings.SplitN(path, \"/\", 2)\n124: \t\tresourceToCheck := \"*/\" + tokens[1]\n125: \t\tif !has(setResources, resourceToCheck) {\n126: \t\t\treturn false\n127: \t\t}\n128: \t}\n129: \n130: \treturn true\n131: }\n132: \n133: func nonResourceURLsCoversAll(set, covers []string) bool {\n134: \tfor _, path := range covers {\n135: \t\tcovered := false\n136: \t\tfor _, owner := range set {\n137: \t\t\tif nonResourceURLCovers(owner, path) {\n138: \t\t\t\tcovered = true\n139: \t\t\t\tbreak\n140: \t\t\t}\n141: \t\t}\n142: \t\tif !covered {\n143: \t\t\treturn false\n144: \t\t}\n145: \t}\n146: \treturn true\n147: }\n148: \n149: func nonResourceURLCovers(ownerPath, subPath string) bool {\n150: \tif ownerPath == subPath {\n151: \t\treturn true\n152: \t}\n153: \treturn strings.HasSuffix(ownerPath, \"*\") && strings.HasPrefix(subPath, strings.TrimRight(ownerPath, \"*\"))\n154: }\n155: \n156: // ruleCovers determines whether the ownerRule (which may have multiple verbs, resources, and resourceNames) covers\n157: // the subrule (which may only contain at most one verb, resource, and resourceName)\n158: func ruleCovers(ownerRule, subRule rbacv1.PolicyRule) bool {\n159: \tverbMatches := has(ownerRule.Verbs, rbacv1.VerbAll) || hasAll(ownerRule.Verbs, subRule.Verbs)\n160: \tgroupMatches := has(ownerRule.APIGroups, rbacv1.APIGroupAll) || hasAll(ownerRule.APIGroups, subRule.APIGroups)\n161: \tresourceMatches := resourceCoversAll(ownerRule.Resources, subRule.Resources)\n162: \tnonResourceURLMatches := nonResourceURLsCoversAll(ownerRule.NonResourceURLs, subRule.NonResourceURLs)\n163: \n164: \tresourceNameMatches := false\n165: \n166: \tif len(subRule.ResourceNames) == 0 {\n167: \t\tresourceNameMatches = (len(ownerRule.ResourceNames) == 0)\n168: \t} else {\n169: \t\tresourceNameMatches = (len(ownerRule.ResourceNames) == 0) || hasAll(ownerRule.ResourceNames, subRule.ResourceNames)\n170: \t}\n171: \n172: \treturn verbMatches && groupMatches && resourceMatches && resourceNameMatches && nonResourceURLMatches\n173: }\n174: multiple layers of validation:\\n\\n1. **Core Escalation Checks (pkg/registry/rbac/escalation_check.go)**: Three main functions enforce escalation restrictions:\\n   - EscalationAllowed() checks if the user belongs to system:masters group (superusers), allowing them to bypass all escalation checks\\n   - RoleEscalationAuthorized() verifies explicit authorization via the 'escalate' verb on role resources. This function creates an AttributesRecord with Verb='escalate' and passes it to the authorizer\\n   - BindingAuthorized() checks if users have explicit authorization to bind specific roles\\n\\n2. **Rule Coverage Validation (pkg/registry/rbac/validation/rule.go)**: The ConfirmNoEscalation() function implements the core escalation prevention by:\\n   - Extracting the user's current permissions from RoleBindings and ClusterRoleBindings\\n   - Using the Covers() function to verify that the rules a user wants to grant are already covered by rules they possess\\n   - Reporting missing permissions that would constitute privilege escalation\\n   - The DefaultRuleResolver class resolves role references to actual policy rules\\n\\n3. **Policy Rule Comparison (staging/src/k8s.io/component-helpers/auth/rbac/validation/policy_comparator.go)**: The Covers() function is the mathematical core:\\n   - Decomposes complex rules into atomic sub-rules via BreakdownRule()\\n   - Checks via ruleCovers() that each sub-rule is covered by at least one owner rule\\n   - Handles wildcards, resource names, subresources (e.g., pods/status), and non-resource URLs\\n   - Returns uncovered rules that would represent escalation\\n\\n4. **Storage Layer Enforcement**: All four RBAC storage implementations enforce escalation checks during Create/Update:\\n   - ClusterRole storage (pkg/registry/rbac/clusterrole/policybased/storage.go): Calls ConfirmNoEscalationInternal() for role rules and special fullAuthority check for aggregation rules\\n   - ClusterRoleBinding storage (pkg/registry/rbac/clusterrolebinding/policybased/storage.go): Calls ConfirmNoEscalation() after checking BindingAuthorized()\\n   - Role storage (pkg/registry/rbac/role/policybased/storage.go): Calls ConfirmNoEscalationInternal() for role rules\\n   - RoleBinding storage (pkg/registry/rbac/rolebinding/policybased/storage.go): Calls ConfirmNoEscalation() after checking BindingAuthorized()\\n\\n5. **Rule Normalization**: Supporting functions prepare rules for comparison:\\n   - ConfirmNoEscalationInternal() (pkg/registry/rbac/validation/internal_version_adapter.go) converts internal version rules to v1 API rules\\n   - CompactRules() (pkg/registry/rbac/validation/policy_compact.go) consolidates simple rules for better error messages\\n   - IsOnlyMutatingGCFields() (pkg/registry/rbac/helpers.go) allows updates that only modify garbage collection metadata\\n\\n6. **Superuser Bypass**: Both mutating admission policy components (pkg/registry/admissionregistration/mutatingadmissionpolicy/authz.go and pkg/registry/admissionregistration/mutatingadmissionpolicybinding/authz.go) use EscalationAllowed() to skip authorization checks for system:masters members\\n\\n7. **Storage Integration**: The RESTStorageProvider (pkg/registry/rbac/rest/storage_rbac.go) wires the DefaultRuleResolver into all policy-based storage implementations, ensuring escalation validation is applied at the API level for all RBAC resource operations.\\n\\nThe key principle is that a user can only grant permissions they already possess - the 'escalate' verb determines if a user can perform this operation directly, while rule coverage ensures the actual permissions granted are within their authority.\"\n}\n","structuredPatch":[],"originalFile":null}}
